Mr. Page Gave a Speech on the Way Out of Capitalism Yesterday

Continuing to Lecture at the YMCA Today

Yesterday was the second day of Mr. Page, an American expert on social issues, giving a lecture. The location was still the auditorium of the YMCA, and the topic was "The Way Out of Capitalism." Despite the heavy rain, the audience was still very enthusiastic. Xu Kesheng presided, Chen Liting translated, and Yang Bingxun took shorthand notes in the national language. The following is an excerpt of his speech: "The motive of capitalism is to greedily seek more profit and develop one's own financial power, so it can also be said to be a selfish and self-serving ideology. Its advantages are: first, raising the standard of living; second, facilitating work; and third, shortening time. These are all the advantages of capitalism. However, its drawbacks lie in: (1) making it impossible for people to enjoy equal benefits, because a few people enjoy great benefits, while the majority are still in poverty; (2) concentrating power, that is, a few people can control great power and arbitrarily monopolize economic power, so that major social undertakings are all affected by them; (3) promoting class warfare, because people are inevitably hostile to each other and hurt each other's feelings under the competitive conditions of the capitalist system, and many people fail as a result, even losing their entire fortune. But how can we avoid these drawbacks? There are now three answers: capitalists say that we already have this capitalist system, so there is no need to change it. Communists advocate using violent means to seize other people's property. Socialists advocate using peaceful methods to improve the social and economic status quo. But what methods should we use? We should now pay attention to: (1) enabling workers to organize solid groups to represent their own interests; (2) enabling workers to organize labor parties like the British Labor Party; (3) using taxation methods to reduce the risks of assets, and there are three types of taxation methods, which Sun Yat-sen also mentioned in his Principle of People's Livelihood: (A) income tax, (B) inheritance tax, and (C) property tax; (4) the state should set a minimum wage; (5) implementing social insurance: (A) sickness insurance, (B) accident insurance,

(C) maternity insurance, (D) old-age insurance, (E) unemployment insurance; (6) all major social production industries should be placed under state management. In short, the Chinese people should currently pay attention to two dangers of Western capitalism: (A) blindly adopting capitalism without thinking; (B) not being able to obtain the benefits of the European and American capitalist systems but instead suffering many harms. I have read Sun Yat-sen's Principle of People's Livelihood and admire it very much, considering it very valuable, because once the problem of people's livelihood is solved, any social problem can be solved easily. In short, we must study how to take its advantages and discard its disadvantages. This afternoon at 5:00 PM, there will be a continuation of the lecture, titled "The End of Imperialism," and all are welcome to participate."

News of Suspension of Navigation on the Upper Yangtze River

Crew Demands Pay Raise and Strikes

The Guowen News Agency reports that various foreign shipping companies stationed in Shanghai received a telegram yesterday stating that all shipping lines on the upper Yangtze River, Yichang-Chongqing route, including Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Nissin and other shipping lines, have been suspended due to a general strike by the crew demanding a pay raise. There is also a tendency for Chinese merchant steamships to join the strike. As a result, the shipment of goods from Shanghai to the upper Yangtze River has been suspended for days.

No Ships Sailed on the Shanghai-Taizhou Route Yesterday

The Guowen News Agency reports that the Zhoushan steamship, which sails on the Shanghai-Taizhou line, usually departs from Shanghai every Monday. Last week, the ship was delayed due to fog and was unable to depart as scheduled. The Dahuang Steamboat, a colleague company, had advanced its schedule to replace it. However, the Zhoushan steamship encountered wind again yesterday and was unable to return to Shanghai on time. It was still possible to request the Dahuang Steamboat to advance its schedule again, but the Dahuang ship suddenly collided with a Wheelock Marden ship when entering the port on the morning of the 2nd. Whether or not it should be repaired is still under investigation, so it is not convenient to sail immediately. Due to these unexpected events, no ships sailed on the Shanghai-Taizhou line yesterday.

Municipal Government to Formulate Regulations on Leasing Wharves for Steamships

The Shanghai Special Municipal Government has formulated rules for steamship companies to lease wharves and warehouse bases in the Nanshi area, which have now been approved and promulgated. The following is a verbatim transcription: (1) Steamship companies in this special municipality that lease wharves and warehouse bases in the Nanshi area shall comply with the provisions of these regulations. (2) The wharves and warehouse bases along the coastline from 16 Pu [Sixteen Shops] in Nanshi to Dongjiadu in the south, except for those designated for public use, shall be approved for lease by steamship companies in accordance with regulations upon application to the Land and Port Affairs Bureau. (3) Steamship companies with three or more self-owned steamships with a total tonnage of 1,500 tons or more may apply to the Land and Port Affairs Bureau for approval to lease wharves and warehouse bases, and pay a deposit in accordance with Articles 4 and 5 below. (4) The amount of the deposit for each wharf south of 16 Pu in Nanshi is set as follows: No. 1, 30,000 yuan; No. 2, 30,000 yuan; No. 3, 30,000 yuan; No. 4, 30,000 yuan; No. 5, 30,000 yuan; No. 6, 30,000 yuan; No. 7, 10,000 yuan; No. 8, 30,000 yuan; No. 10, 20,000 yuan; No. 13, 25,000 yuan; No. 14, 25,000 yuan; No. 15, 25,000 yuan; No. 16, 25,000 yuan; No. 17, 20,000 yuan. (5) The amount of the deposit for each warehouse south of 16 Pu in Nanshi is 20,000 yuan; No. 3, 40,000 yuan; No. 4, 30,000 yuan; No. 5, 30,000 yuan; No. 6, 60,000 yuan; No. 9, 20,000 yuan. (6) The total amount of the deposit is set at 700,000 yuan. From January 1, 1931, half of the amount, totaling 350,000 yuan, will be returned to the shipping companies within five years, at a rate of 70,000 yuan per year, with the end of December each year as the date for the refund. The remaining half will be kept as a long-term deposit. (7) The interest rate on the deposit is 5% per annum, payable semi-annually, with June 30 and December 31 of each year as the dates for interest payment. (8) When leasing wharves and warehouse bases, steamship companies must submit a statement to the Port Affairs Bureau and the Land Bureau respectively. After the location and term of use have been approved by the Port Affairs Bureau and the Land Bureau, a contract will be signed. However, the term of lease shall not exceed 15 years, and may be renewed for another 15 years upon expiration. (9) After the amount of the deposit has been approved by the Port Affairs Bureau and the Land Bureau, the Finance Bureau will be notified by letter, and the steamship company will be notified at the same time to pay directly to the Finance Bureau, which will issue a receipt. If this receipt is lost, the Finance Bureau, the Land Bureau, and the Port Affairs Bureau shall be notified immediately for record, and a public announcement shall be made to request a replacement. (10) If the lease of the wharf and warehouse base is not renewed after the expiration of the term, half of the long-term deposit will be refunded in full.

Gold and Goods Exchanges to Close on Sundays

The gold and goods exchanges in this port have a significant impact on the market. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has previously investigated and determined that there are no exchange rates to rely on on Sundays, so they should be closed to avoid speculation and disruption of the market. After receiving the order, the exchanges have consulted several times and decided to comply with the order starting this week (the 2nd). Therefore, the market was not open on the 2nd and there were no market prices.

Ambush Case on Jing'an Temple Road Last Night

Enemies Lying in Wait by the Roadside, Zhang Yuanmu Suffers an Unexpected Calamity, Chopped Five Times with an Axe, Bleeding Profusely, Unconscious Upon Arrival at the Hospital

Zhang Yuanmu, a local resident, 29 years old, was walking along Jing'an Temple Road at 9:35 last night when he was suddenly ambushed by enemies lying in wait by the roadside. Upon seeing Zhang arrive, they attacked him without asking any questions, wielding sharp axes and chopping him twice on the head, once on the face, and once on each hand, for a total of five chops. He immediately collapsed to the ground, bleeding profusely. When nearby patrol officers No. 1931 and No. 1471 heard the alarm and came to the scene, the perpetrators had already fled. They immediately took Zhang to Renji Hospital for treatment. He was unconscious and his injuries were critical. Zhang was wearing a camel hair robe, a short flannel shirt, blue silk pants, satin shoes, and white socks.

Xiyin Clock on Weiting Mountain

He Yushu Presents Clock to Farmers

He Yushu, Director of the Agricultural and Mining Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, recently visited the rural service center established by the Suzhou Youth Association on Weiting Mountain. He greatly praised the various works. Seeing that the existing time-telling clock on the mountain had poor sound, he specifically donated a large bronze bell, named the "Xiyin [Cherish Time] Clock." The bell has recently been cast and transported to the mountain. The villagers held a grand bell-hanging ceremony to welcome it, with gongs and cannons, which was quite lively. The bell has now been hung high on Weiting Mountain and rings three times a day, allowing farmers in more than twenty villages around to know the accurate time.

Teacher at Tiantong Middle School Attempts Suicide Out of Shame and Anger After Lover Elopes

Drinks Liquor and Inhales Smoke, Despairing of Life, Landlord Discovers and Sends to Hospital for Treatment

Wang Shikun, 28 years old, from Nanjing, unmarried, rented a room at No. 39 Yuanmaoli, Tiantong Road. He taught at Tiantong Middle School in nearby Tiantongli. In August of last year, Wang met a local woman, Ms. So-and-so. Friendship led to love, and they made a vow of lifelong commitment. They then held a banquet at the Shanghai Hotel on Guangdong Road and began cohabiting. Their relationship was extremely harmonious. Half a year passed quickly. However, four days ago, Ms. So-and-so suddenly eloped. Wang sent scouts to search everywhere, but to no avail. Feeling ashamed to face others, Wang became depressed and suddenly had suicidal thoughts. Yesterday, after finishing his classes at 4:00 PM, he returned to his residence, drank a large amount of liquor, and inhaled smoke. Soon, his complexion turned pale. The landlord happened to notice and quickly reported to Tiandao Middle School, which reported to the Third Precinct of the Fifth District, ordering the police to accompany him to Xiangren Hospital for treatment. Husband Chops Concubine's Lover on Yangzhou Road

Wife Returns Home and Finds Another Love, Unable to Suppress Anger, Wields Knife and Attacks

Ye Zhiqing, from Shaoxing, because at noon on the 2nd of this month, he went to the house at No. 1107 Yangzhou Road and used a kitchen knife to wound the head of Jiang Youde, a fellow townsman, was arrested by Hua police officer No. 2269 and detective Shan Zhaoxian from the Yangshupu Police Station, who rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm. Ye was arrested along with the kitchen knife and his wife, Chen, and taken to the police station for detention. The police also ordered the injured person to be taken to the hospital for treatment. Ye Zhiqing claimed at the police station that the injured person and his wife Chen had committed adultery. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Xu Jiaxi came to the Seventh Court to investigate, and the police lawyer Gan Jingxian stated the case, saying that the victim was unable to appear in court because he was in the hospital and requested a postponement. Detective Wu Bingliang testified that he was the landlord of the house, and that Ye Chen and her mother lived upstairs. The injured person Jiang Youde often came, but he did not know about the adultery between Jiang Youde and Ye Chen. He was not at home when the incident happened yesterday afternoon, and only found out later. Chen Jintai testified that Ye Chen was his younger sister. Last May, she had a quarrel with her husband Ye Zhiqing and gave birth to a child, who died a few days later. He blamed his sister for intentionally killing the child, so she returned home and refused to go back. On December 25th of last year, Ye Zhiqing came to his house to invite his sister back, but his mother refused because his family was impoverished and unable to support her. Before this incident, his mother had gone to Hangzhou to burn incense and had not returned. He did not know whether his sister had an affair with the injured person. Yesterday afternoon, he, his two brothers, and the injured person were having lunch when the defendant suddenly arrived, attacked Jiang Youde's head twice with a kitchen knife without asking any questions, and he fell to the ground. The police arrested him after being notified. Questioned, the defendant Ye Zhiqing confessed that he had been married to Chen for three years. Last May, she gave birth to a child who died soon after. Afterwards, she despised him and complained that he was poor, so she used the excuse of returning to her mother's house in Ningbo to work in a yarn factory and never returned. In August of that year, he went to his mother-in-law's house to get clothes, but his mother-in-law accused him of being a robber and reported him to the police. The police inquired about the situation and did not arrest him. Later, on February 25, he went to his father-in-law's house again, intending to take his wife to rent a house in Minhang. He was going there for some business and his wife Chen said if they were to live together it would have to be in the next life. His mother-in-law was very fierce and his father-in-law, although not outwardly disapproving, was powerless to insist. Yesterday morning at 11 o'clock, he went to see his wife for some reason, sneaked upstairs, and saw his wife and Jiang Youde sleeping together. They were unaware of his presence. Overcome with anger, he went downstairs to a friend's house and stole a kitchen knife, then returned and saw Jiang Youde, his wife's brothers, and his wife Chen having lunch, so he attacked Jiang Youde's head twice with the kitchen knife. Questioned, Ye Chen confessed that she was accused by the defendant for purposely killing their baby. and that she was being threatened and that was why she returned to her mother's house. Because Ye would not support her she went to work in a factory to earn wages. Because she had been sickly, Jiang had helped her by loaning her money, thus she had become lovers with him. She denied sleeping together with Jiang at 11 a.m. that morning, that the defendant's claims were completely false, and that she would return with the defendant if he could financially provide for her, and was willing to do so. Judge Xu reviewed the confessions, ordered the two defendants to be returned to detention separately, and ordered that Jiang Youde be interrogated again after he recovered from his injuries.

Russian Man Opens Fire After Drinking Without Reason

Small Workers Frightened and Flee, Sentenced to a Fine of 30 Yuan

However, the Russian was addicted to alcohol and often went out alone to drink. The other day, in the morning, Ke left a Russian bar at No. 8 Tongfu Road, heavily drunk. While walking along Dagu Road, he became excited from the alcohol and took out a pistol from his side, firing it into the air six times in a row. Several small workers were passing by at the time and, fearing being hit by stray bullets, ran away in panic. They found one bullet in the barrel and a cartridge box and two gun licenses on his person. He was taken to the Provisional Court yesterday for questioning. The Russian man confessed that he was drunk and lost consciousness at the time, which is why he acted that way, and asked for leniency. Judge Luo reviewed the confession and sentenced the Russian man to a fine of 30 yuan as a warning.

West Gate Collapsed House Case, Summons for Owner to Attend

Children Plead With Mother to Return Home

Gu Qingnian's Utmost Sincerity

Gu Zhou, an old woman from Yancheng, now 57 years old, secretly came to Shanghai to work as a servant 30 years ago after quarreling with her husband, Gu Changfu. She had a son and a daughter at home, who have now grown up, married, and have children of their own. After coming to Shanghai, Zhou had an affair with a young man and had a son and a daughter with him. The young man treated her very well. Her husband had previously come to Shanghai to persuade her to return home, but she refused. Now, Gu Changfu has died of illness in the past year. Her son, Qingnian, has repeatedly sent letters asking his mother to come home, but to no avail. He came to Shanghai with his sister the other day, found his mother in a bungalow at No. 379 Guangzhao Road in Zhabei, and greeted his mother. After being separated for more than 30 years, they hugged each other and wept bitterly, urging their mother to return home with them. However, Zhou refused, saying that her lover was currently unemployed and that all the money she had saved from her work, several hundred yuan, had been used up, but he had treated her well and she also had children with him, so she could not abandon them halfway and return to her hometown with her son. Her son Qingnian was very frustrated to hear this, so he and his sister prepared to sleep in front of his mother's door that night, determined to persuade their mother to return home with them. They also asked their mother to bring her lover and younger siblings back to their hometown and provide for them as usual. Qingnian and his sister cried loudly in front of the door. The local defense corps and patrol officers, hearing about Qingnian's commendable filial piety, have already been trying to persuade his mother to return home with her son in order to reunite with the family.

Failing to Report Death of Child Bride, Coffin Opened for Autopsy Yesterday, Determined to be Death From Sickness

Shen Tangfu and his wife Shen Huang, from Suzhou, operate a rowing boat business at the Santai Wharf in Nanshi. They have a daughter named Gendi, 17 years old, who was promised to the family of Zhou Shenglin, a fellow townsman and boat operator in Pudong, as a child bride. She moved into their home, but on January 20 of this year, Gendi suddenly died. Zhou did not report the death and hastily had her buried in a desolate grave. After Shen Tangfu learned of this, and after people exaggerated the story, saying that Zhou Shenglin intended to assault the child bride, the attempt failed, and he murdered her. Shen was deeply saddened and reported it to the Water Patrol Police Station, who sent detectives to arrest Zhou and his mistress Xu Lu, and turn them over to the local court for detention. The other day, the local court ordered bailiff Yin Daoxu to escort both parties to the Yizhong [righteous burial] land, about three miles north of Yangjing in Pudong, where the coffin was found in the mud. Hired workers carried it to the court. The judge ordered an autopsy to be performed the next day. Yesterday at 10:00 AM, Prosecutor Li, along with members from the autopsy office examined the remains. After opening the coffin, which was discovered in the mud, it was transported to court. The corpse, dressed in two old black cotton jackets, two old blue cloth shirts, a patched blue cloth trousers, a pair of black cloth cotton shoes, and a black velvet hat. After a thorough examination, the injuries sustained by the deceased in her hands and feet were very slight and did not appear to be lethal, that the death was due to sickness. After the examination, both parties confessed and Prosecutor Li adjourned the trial, ordered both parties to sign a bond, and the plaintiff was dismissed and the defendant ordered to be detained.

Three Large Packages of Opium in Crotch

Sun Yulin, a patrol officer from the First Precinct of the Nanshi First District, led patrol officers He Yuming and Yang Hongzhen to patrol the Limmalu area of Dongjiadu yesterday morning at 11:00 AM. They saw two rickshaws speeding towards them. The passengers on board, seeing the police, suddenly looked flustered. Suspecting that they were suspicious, they immediately stopped them and ordered them to be searched. They found three large packages of opium, weighing about sixty taels, in the crotches of the two men. They took the people and the evidence back to the station. The station chief ordered them to be interrogated. One man confessed that his name was Zeng Guangfeng, 34 years old, from Hubei, and he worked as a tea boy on the Puzhong Daheng steamship at Dongjiadu. The other man confessed that his name was Wang Chenglin, 42 years old, a fellow townsman of Zeng Guangfeng, and he also worked on the same steamship. They then confessed that the opium was transported from their hometown to Shanghai, totaling four large packages, intending to sell them. However, one package was seized by the customs officers, leaving these three packages, which were then discovered. The station chief, considering that the case involved smuggling opium, which is prohibited, ordered that a document be prepared along with the seized evidence and sent to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation and punishment.

Police Investigate Firearms in Coffins

Xu Jishi, captain of the Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, learned that bandits recently hid firearms in empty coffins, parked them in remote places and on the banks of the Huangpu River, and transported them as coffins, which has a significant impact on local security. He has specifically ordered the patrol officers and chiefs of all sub-teams to pay attention, go to remote locations near Qiujiang Bridge and near the banks of the Huangpu River to conduct investigations, and strictly crack down on them.

Gambling Using Magnetism

Dice Contain Iron Filings, Purely Fraudulent

Shen Defu, Chief Inspector of the French Concession Detective, inspectors Chen Sanlin, detective Lu Jinchen, Lu Jinbao, Mao Jinsheng, Bao Tan Jiang Changwen, and others, learned that someone had privately set up a large gambling den at No. 295 Avenue Edward VII, gathering people to gamble and profiting from skimming, in violation of the ban. Therefore, they immediately went to the location without making a sound, seized gambling equipment such as Pai Gow, shaking dice, betting board, and silver dollars, arrested more than forty gamblers, and took them, along with the boss He Rongsheng, to the police station. After being interrogated by the police chief, the gamblers were given light fines and dismissed. He was handed over for investigation. Yesterday, he was sent to the French Concession Court for investigation. First, Western Inspector Xia Caier claimed that the defendant's gambling equipment, the dice, contained iron filings, and there was a magnet under the betting board, which was purely fraudulent, violating Article 280 of the criminal law, and requested a severe punishment. Questioned, He confessed to privately gathering gamblers and profiting from skimming. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced He to a fine of 200 yuan, and if he was unable to pay the fine, he would be imprisoned for 200 days as a warning. The gambling equipment and silver dollars were confiscated.

Merchant Ship Damaged by Steamer

Over One Hundred Boxes of Kerosene Lost

Yesterday at approximately 3:00 PM, a Shandong vessel carrying 4,000 boxes of kerosene, intending to sail to Zhejiang province for delivery, had just sailed south of the 16th dock of the Pujiang River in the Nanshi area, when it was unexpectedly struck head-on by a certain Japanese merchant steamer. Due to the strong wind, it was impossible to avoid the collision, resulting in damage to the cargo ship's hull and the loss of

over one hundred boxes of kerosene. Afterwards, the ship owner reported the incident to the water police station and other authorities for record-keeping, in order to negotiate and recover the losses.

Shipping Representatives Request Clear Definition of Dock Locations and Widths

Xing Zhigang and others, representatives of shipping businesses in Pudong and Puxi, yesterday submitted a document to the Municipal Port Authority, stating that they respectfully request the clear definition of the locations and widths of public docks south of the Wanyu Dock, in order to maintain shipping operations. They stated that the Nanshi commercial district relies heavily on trade with various inland cities and towns, so the transportation of goods

relies mainly on ships. If there are no public docks to moor at, then goods cannot be loaded or unloaded, and the Nanshi commercial district will decline as a result. Even considering rural ships, after arriving in Shanghai, if there are no reliable docks, they must anchor far out in the river and transfer goods ashore with great difficulty and frequent danger. This cannot be ignored. They recently read in the newspaper that the entire Pudong shoreline is managed by the Authority, and is being leased to various shipping companies. There is barely any space left for the original docks in Nanshi, and the locations of the public docks have yet to be defined. Various businesses and ship associations are deeply concerned about this. They fear that shipping companies will monopolize the shoreline rights, completely blocking the existing docks, and placing the Nanshi merchants relying on inland trade and the rural ships transporting goods in an impossible situation. This is deeply concerning. Furthermore, the Wanyu Dock and the Nanhui Guildhall Dock are the most important docks along the Pudong waterfront, traditionally serving as mooring places for ships sailing between Pudong and Puxi. Other docks such as the Yongsheng Dock and the Santai Dock are also well-known shipping hubs. In order to maintain the transportation and livelihoods of millions of people along the Pudong waterfront, the representatives feel compelled to explain the situation. They jointly submit this report to the Authority, hoping that the Authority will investigate and approve the prompt definition and announcement of the locations and widths of the public docks south of the Wanyu Dock, in order to maintain shipping operations and reassure the public. They will be eternally grateful.

Collision Between Dahua Steamer and Towing Barge

Dahua Steamer Damaged in Collision

The Dahua steamer, belonging to the Nanshi Ping'an Company's Haimen line, was carrying passengers from Haimen to Shanghai the day before yesterday afternoon. As it sailed past the Shanghai Waterworks Plant in Yangshupu, between buoys twelve and thirteen, a towing barge belonging to the Jardine Matheson Company was turning a large steamer around. The Dahua steamer attempted to avoid it by steering towards Puxi, but the towing barge also moved towards Puxi. The two vessels were very close to each other, and could not avoid colliding. The bow of the Dahua steamer was immediately damaged. The steamer then returned to its company and reported the incident. The company has submitted a request to the customs authorities, asking them to negotiate with the Jardine Matheson Company for compensation for the damages.

Cesspit in Xue Family Garden

Whether to Renovate Awaiting Inspection

Xue Baorun, a wealthy businessman residing on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, was previously reported to the French Municipal Council by the French Municipal Bureau, for having two vats in his garden emitting foul odors that were detrimental to hygiene. They requested that the vats be dismantled and replaced with Western-style cesspools. He was ordered to renovate the cesspools in a Western style. Yesterday, the deadline was reached and he was summoned again. An employee of the Municipal Bureau stated that the cesspools in the defendant's garden had still not been renovated, and that he was deliberately disobeying the order. They requested an investigation. A certain person surnamed Xue arrived on Xue Baorun's behalf, stating that after receiving the order, the defendant had completely renovated the cesspools according to the Municipal Bureau's designs, and that the original cesspools had long been filled in and could be inspected. The Chinese and Western officials stated that since both sides held differing opinions, they would await a clear inspection before further questioning.

Woman Struck by Iron Hammer Dies of Her Injuries

Cao Gao, a woman from Pudong, age 22, was struck in the head with an iron hammer by her fellow townsman Wang Bingqian on Dalianwan Road on the afternoon of the first of this month. Bleeding profusely, she fell to the ground and cried for help. Police officers who heard the call apprehended Wang and took him into custody at the Huishan Police Station. The injured woman was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but she died of excessive blood loss at 7:00 AM yesterday. The police station immediately summoned witnesses and took the suspect to the Provisional Court, where Judge Xu questioned him. Witnesses Gui Wu, Wu Qianmei, and others testified that they lived near the scene of the incident and were cooking lunch at the time. Hearing cries for help, they went out to see what was happening and saw a woman on the ground. The assailant was straddling her and beating her with his fists. They tried to stop him, and he fled. They helped the woman up, but her head was bleeding profusely. Fortunately, the detectives arrived and apprehended the assailant. The victim's husband, Cao Ziqing, stated that he married Gao in November of the year before last and currently lives in Chunyangli, Beikaier Road. Questioned about this, the defendant stated that Gao's mother, Zhao, had been his mistress for ten years, since Gao was only

twelve years old. He raised her entirely, and sent her to school as she grew older. In September of the fifteenth year of the Republic, he went to another city and separated from her mother and daughter. On the second day of the first month of last year, he returned to Shanghai from Yichang and learned that A-Quan (the deceased's name) had married, and that her mother, Zhao, was also living with her son-in-law. At the end of last year, he encountered the daughter in front of a certain cigarette factory. When he called out to her, she refused to acknowledge that he was her father. During the Lantern Festival, he encountered the daughter again at the Xia Hai Temple with her husband, Cao Ziqing, who were burning incense, and called out to her again, but she still ignored him. The day before yesterday, he encountered her again, and she still ignored him and cursed at him. Angered, he struck her with an iron hammer. Upon hearing Wang's testimony, Cao Ziqing immediately declared that the defendant's claim of burning incense at the Xia Hai Temple was entirely fabricated, and that his mother-in-law did not live with them. Judge Xu ordered the defendant to be detained pending further investigation.

Robbers in Candy Store Heist Arrested

Detectives from the Municipal Public Security Bureau learned that Xu Wenfu (also known as Xu Gengen, nicknamed "Leather Shoe Gengen"), a local robber involved in the robbery of over 27,000 silver dollars from the Shouhe Kangji Candy Store in Xiaodongmen on January 19, 1927, was hiding at the Ziyang Inn, 32 Hankou Road. The bureau then requested assistance from the Laozha Police Station the night before last, and the chief dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to arrest Xu. He was taken to the Provisional Court yesterday, and witness Zhang Hongyuan was summoned. Zhang testified that his father, Songquan, had been the mistress of Zhu Tao's sister. The Xiaodongmen candy store robbery had been committed by his father and Zhu, among others. After the robbery, they went to his house to divide the loot, and the defendant, Leather Shoe Gengen, was also present. He witnessed them taking out guns, as many as seven of them. Last year, when the Public Security Bureau sent officers to search his house, his father was not found, so he was detained. He was recently released on bail. Xu denied the charges, claiming that he was being framed. Judge Gao ordered the defendant to be detained pending further investigation by the Public Security Bureau.

Jin Bogeng Arrested for Extortion

Seeing Women, He Just Wanted to Get Rich

After the Shanghai Wing On Textile Mill took over the Zhonghua Textile Mill in Wusong, it was renamed the Wing On Second Textile Mill. Due to a shortage of female workers, they sent female foremen Zhang Huo and He Huo from Changzhou to recruit 15 female workers. They arrived in Shanghai by train the day before yesterday and stayed at the Datong Inn on North Zhejiang Road. Yesterday at 11:00 AM, the factory sent employee Pan Weizhang to the inn to pay the travel expenses. He then accompanied the female workers to the Huaxing Restaurant on Huaxing Road for lunch. At that time, Jin Bogeng from Hunan was also having lunch at the restaurant. Seeing Pan with over twenty young women, he suspected that they had come by improper means and intended to extort fifty dollars, claiming that he was a relative of Commander Chiang and was currently a detective. Pan, who was busy, did not want to argue with him and agreed to pay for the meal, but Jin refused. Pan called the police, and they took Jin to the First Precinct of the Fourth District. After hearing the story, Chief Ni determined that Jin had impersonated a government official and extorted money, and that he could not be lenient. He prepared a document to send to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Two Old Men Fight Over Small Amount of Money

Six Jiao Causes Them to Come to Blows

Their Difficult Lives Are Truly Pitiable

Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, two old men with white hair and beards were fighting on Yaojia Stone Bridge Road in Zhabei. Police officers from the nearby checkpoint tried to break up the fight, but they refused to stop, so they were taken to the Fourth District Headquarters. One of the men, Liu Rulin, an old man of seventy years, cowered and said, "I owe Zhang Jinbiao six jiao. I intended to pay it back, but lately I have had bad luck and have been unemployed for several years. My pockets are empty, and I have no choice but to beg for a living. I don't even have money for food. I met Zhang Jinbiao on the road, and he insisted on collecting the debt. I pleaded with him, but he refused to show mercy and beat me. Please investigate." As he spoke, tears streamed down his face, showing his misery. Zhang Jinbiao, age 55, said, "I was asking him for money, but I didn't mean to force him. It's just that I am also down on my luck and have been hungry for days. In a moment of anger, I punched him a few times. Please forgive me." The chief ruled that the two old men were arguing over a small amount of money, which was truly pitiable. He ordered them to reconcile outside, but since Zhang had used violence and violated police regulations, he was fined two dollars as a warning.

Four Deaths

One Suicide... Three Died of Illness

A rickshaw puller commits suicide. Tao Youqi, a 45-year-old tenant living on the third floor of Mao A'er's house at No. 5 Taiyuan Lane at the entrance to Lin Yin Road outside Ximen, worked as a rickshaw puller. He worked hard the day before yesterday and earned two hundred copper coins, intending to use them for firewood and rice. Unexpectedly, they were stolen on the road by a thief. When Tao returned home and searched for the copper coins, they were gone. He resented his bad luck, thinking that it would never end, and that he was getting old. Although he had a son, he could not support his aging father. Filled with resentment, he thought that it was better to die than live, and hanged himself in his room. Yesterday morning, the second landlord found him already dead. He reported it to the Second District Police Station, which ordered the Thirteen Tutelary of the Twenty-fifth Bao, Dong Qing, to report it to the local court. Prosecutor Yang and others arrived to examine the body and ordered it to be collected.

A suspect dies of illness. Guo Jiheng, a native of Zhejiang, was arrested in September of the 16th year of the Republic for robbery. He was arrested by the Dixiwei Road Police Station and sent to court for questioning. He was sentenced to twelve years in prison. Recently, he fell ill in prison and was transferred to the infirmary. He died at 7:30 AM yesterday. The police station took the body to the Philander Road Morgue and reported it to the Provisional Court. Judge Sun Yuan arrived at noon and determined that the deceased had died of illness. Since he had no family, the body was handed over to the Pushan Cemetery for burial.

A male corpse found dead on the road. An unnamed male corpse, about twenty years old, was found at 3:00 AM on the second of this month in Lanfang Lane at the intersection of Huolun Mill Street and Caishi Street in the French Concession. The corpse was covered in mud. The doorman of the alley, Zhang Jinlan, reported it to the Big Bell Police Station. The chief sent detectives to investigate. The corpse was bald, barefoot, naked from the waist up, wearing white cloth trousers covered by blue cloth cotton trousers. Beside him were a short blue willow-patterned white cloth shirt. One gold tooth was embedded in the upper stone surface of his mouth. His head, face, and chest were covered in mud. There were bloodstains on his chest and nose, indicating that he had been injured. He had no family. The detectives reported back to the chief, who ordered the body to be taken to the Tongren Fuyuantang Mortuary. Yesterday, the Criminal Division of the French Police Station reported to Judge Zhu Cheng of the French Court, who determined that the deceased had died for some reason on the road. He ordered that the body be photographed and that the Tongren Fuyuantang provide a coffin and collect the body.

Death from illness in a hotel. Li Minxuan, a native of Guangdong, age 26, was a former soldier who had recently retired. He was passing through Shanghai on his way home and stayed at the Deji Inn at 217 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. He fell ill at the inn and died suddenly at 6:00 AM on the second of this month. The inn's tea server, Li Changqing, reported it to the police station, who sent detectives to investigate. The corpse was wearing a silk Guangben factory thread-padded jacket and trousers, covered by a gray cotton military uniform, with a sanitary shirt and Western-style trousers underneath. He had a leather trouser belt around his waist. A certificate of discharge for officers and soldiers of the Fifth Route Army before the disbandment of the Wuhan Branch of the Central Military Academy was found in his pocket, as well as a piece of white cloth with the words "Fifth Team, Second Squad" written on it, and a wooden seal with the inscription "Li Yuxuan". There was nothing else. The detectives took the belongings back to the police station and reported to the chief, who ordered the body to be taken to the Tongren Fuyuantang Mortuary. Yesterday, the Criminal Division of the French Police Station reported to Judge Zhu Cheng of the French Court, who determined that the deceased had died of illness. Since he had no family, he ordered that the body be photographed and that the Tongren Fuyuantang provide a coffin and collect the body.

Zhang Jiaxian Hangs Himself After Drinking

Zhang Jiaxian, a native of Zhenjiang, age 34, was a salesman at the Dechang Foreign Goods Store at 65 Fuxing Lane, Beijing Road. Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, Zhang collected one dollar in salary from the store's accounting office and went out to have fun. Around 5:00 PM, he passed the Zhang Dongming Wine Shop, went inside, and bought some wine to drink alone. He seemed quite relaxed and had a slight buzz. He hired a streetcar, agreeing to pay one hundred coins for the fare. When he arrived at the store, he chatted and laughed with the accounting office staff, enjoying himself. Before dinner, his colleagues invited him to join them, but he said that he was full and tired and wanted to go to his room to sleep. After entering his room, he bolted the door. His colleagues did not suspect anything unusual. Around 7:00 PM, a Mr. Mou from the accounting office wanted to put on his clothes to go home and went to his room to retrieve his belongings. Finding the door closed and receiving no response after knocking several times, he became suspicious. He found a way to pry open the door and went into the room, where he saw Zhang hanging from the iron bed frame. He was breathing rapidly and his pulse had stopped. They quickly ordered someone to take him down, and summoned a doctor, but it was no use. Around 9:00 PM, they took him to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but as of midnight last night, he was still in danger.

Confiscated Vehicles to Be Auctioned Off at Reduced Prices

It is said that two private rickshaws, five business rickshaws, five large trucks, two small trucks, and four small vehicles remain. The bureau has resubmitted a request to the municipal government to approve the redetermination of prices and reschedule the auction due to the long-term storage of the vehicles and the ease with which they can be damaged.

The following resolutions were passed: A. The name will be the Shanghai Special City Furnace Industry Association. B.

The old name will be immediately abolished, and the powers will be exercised in the name of the trade association. C. (2) In accordance with Articles 3 and 4 of the Industry and Commerce Law, a list of the names of the members of the trade must be prepared and submitted to the competent Social Affairs Bureau for registration, in order to facilitate contact and enable members to enjoy the public benefits of maintaining and promoting the interests and correcting the malpractices of the industry. The New Taikoo Godown Workers' Union held its eighth executive committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Yang Mingwei. In his report, the chairman stated that during the recent labor-management dispute, representatives demanded that the company resume work to maintain the workers' livelihoods, which the company agreed to. The union was extremely fortunate to receive assistance from various higher-level godowns and unions. He hoped that our workers would work diligently, and that labor and management would benefit mutually. Regarding propaganda matters, Hu Peiqing was responsible for weekly union propaganda to ensure that workers understand the party's labor movement and liberation of the people. In addition, the collection of monthly dues was the responsibility of each group leader to remit to the accountant, and those who have not paid should be urged to pay to benefit the union. The meeting adjourned. Acknowledgment: We received from the Commercial Press one copy each of the "Students' Magazine," Volume 16, No. 11, and the "Women's Magazine," Volume 15, No. 10. Thank you.

Incoming Correspondence

Shanghai Special Municipality Municipal Government Report (III) (Republic of China Year 18) 7. On Sanitary Administration Matters Sanitary administration is extremely important, as it concerns the health and well-being of citizens. The work carried out in the past year can be summarized as follows: (1) Expanding sanitary services: to promote the development of rural sanitation, a model sanitary district has been established in the Wusong District of Puxi and the Gaoqiao District of Pudong. The intention is to gradually implement this in other districts. To promote the development of physical education, school health services were created. By the end of the eighteenth year of the Republic, a total of 10,894 students had received medical treatment, 8,638 students had undergone health examinations, 1,115 students had their dental diseases treated, and 1,563 students had their minor eye diseases treated. To promote the prosperity of medicine, public hospitals were improved, mobile clinics were established, registration of public and private hospitals and physicians and pharmacists continued, and two sanitary campaigns were held in May and December of the previous year to spread sanitary knowledge among citizens. (2) Preventing the spread of epidemics: free smallpox vaccinations were administered. In the eighteenth year, a total of 129,978 people were vaccinated. Free cholera vaccinations were administered. In the eighteenth year, a total of 131,173 people were vaccinated. The names, origins, transmission, main symptoms, treatments, and preventive measures for important seasonal diseases were compiled into concise tables and distributed for posting to broaden public awareness. (3) Rectifying sanitation matters: the cleanliness of city streets is crucial for sanitation. Regulations for rectifying sanitation were established. The Sanitary Bureau hired 503 street sweepers and 18 sanitary inspectors, along with 8 managers, to manage different areas and be responsible for sweeping. All garbage dumps and landfill areas were covered with coal ash to prevent pollution. (4) Conducting livestock inspections: The meat of pigs, sheep, and cattle is essential for the daily consumption of citizens. If meat from livestock with epidemic diseases is sold under false pretenses, it can easily cause illness. Therefore, inspecting livestock for epidemic diseases is an important task of municipal sanitary work. In the previous year, regulations for inspecting livestock for slaughter were revised to ensure compliance. Pig slaughter inspections were originally carried out in Nanshi and Zhabei. Now, they have been extended to Jiangwan, Zhenru, Wusong, Pusong, Fahua, and Yangjing districts. By the end of the eighteenth year, a total of 1,015,436 pigs were inspected, and 7,259 diseased pigs were found to be unfit for consumption. Inspections for slaughtered and sold cattle and sheep began in October of the eighteenth year. A total of 15,219 cattle were inspected, and 110 diseased cattle were found. A total of 14,043 sheep were inspected, and 13 diseased sheep were found. 8. On Educational Administration Matters Education is fundamental to the establishment of a nation. The city has a dense population and thriving commerce and industry. School education and social education both need to be actively promoted. The work carried out in the past year can be summarized as follows: (1) Regarding school education: implement the Three Principles of the People education, prepare for compulsory education in phases, establish kindergartens in different districts, establish experimental primary schools, reorganize private schools, improve private universities, organize summer research institutes for teachers and staff, educational research associations, and travel and tour groups, organize Boy Scouts, survey school-age children in the city, register primary school teachers, continue intelligence tests and educational tests, implement college counseling, repair school buildings in phases, hold the Second Primary School Joint Sports Meet, organize a curriculum research committee for primary and secondary schools, reorganize the joint associations of teachers and staff of various schools, and handle school health matters. (2) Regarding social education: conduct literacy campaigns, organize public education committees, promote public education, establish agricultural and industrial supplementary schools, install public reading boards, establish simple public education centers. In addition, the assessment of primary school teachers, preparation for the city-wide sports meet, compilation of the city gazetteer, promotion of compulsory education, insurance and repair of school buildings, holding school equipment exhibitions, organizing educational and cultural groups, and building concert halls, increasing city school grades are all in progress.

9. On Public Utilities Matters Public utilities such as water supply, electricity, and land and water transportation are essential to national civilization and the well-being of the people, and are also the foundation of municipal construction. The work carried out in the past year can be summarized as follows: (1) Regarding water supply: facilitate the laying of 18,780 feet of 18-inch diameter large water pipes in the new western district; facilitate the connection of running water to Jiangwan; resolve the issue of silk factories in the Rihui Port area paying fees to connect to water pipes; facilitate the connection of water pipes to Tanziwan; supervise the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to lay pipes and connect Yinxiang; conduct water supply registration; supervise inland water companies to improve water plant equipment; revise the third water pipe contract of the French Concession Water Plant and sign the fourth water pipe contract, and comply with the municipal government's order contract (detailed in the "Compilation of Sino-French Water and Electricity Negotiations," original book attached); prohibit residents in the Chinese-concession boundary from arbitrarily connecting to the Concession's running water; facilitate the connection of water pipes between Chinese and foreign water plants in the city; and coordinate water outages. (2) Regarding electricity: supervise the Zhabei power plant project; inspect five types of light bulbs, including Yabuer Leiting, Philips, Yasiling, and GE; conduct registration of electrical users, wiremen, and apprentices; facilitate Xianghua Electric Company purchasing electricity from Zhabei Water and Electricity Company; abolish connection fees and meter maintenance fees; reduce electricity and lighting fees; prohibit power outages; recover and prohibit the supply of electricity beyond boundaries; and review the fuel of electricity companies such as coal, water, and oil. (3) Regarding land and water transportation: reorganize the Wusong River ferry; build the Pudong River ferry, Donggou Wharf; build the first municipal ferry; order the second ferry; establish the Wusong Shipping Office; inspect ships; promote public buses; conduct registration of automobile drivers and gas stations; install rickshaw parking signs; and prohibit foreign merchants from driving electric vehicles into the Chinese area. (4) Regarding other public utilities: take over streetlights in Yinxiang and Wusong districts; establish the Wusong Streetlight Management Office; re-determine streetlight on/off times; build and reorganize public advertising spaces; sign public advertising space contracts with Zhongxing Advertising Company and Kangtai Advertising Company; conclude the door number compilation; and negotiate and sign contracts with Shanghai Lame Fire Company.

The above nine points highlight the most prominent ones. As for this year's policy directions,

we must恪遵 the teachings of the Premier, uphold the guidance of the National Government and the Party Headquarters, and strive to implement the construction work during the tutelage period. To complete the plan for Greater Shanghai, we must actively construct the city center area and build the city's main roads. To improve finance, we must reduce the burden on citizens by increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. To reorganize land, we must continue to rush to conduct land surveys and implement equal land rights. To develop the social economy, we must support industry and commerce, protect tenant farmers, and improve the lives of workers. To consolidate local security, we must actively strengthen preparedness and improve police standards. To improve the health of citizens, we must improve sanitary services and carry out cleanliness campaigns. To popularize education, we must focus on compulsory education and expand public schools. To benefit the citizens, we must reorganize water, electricity, and other public utilities. It is hoped that the Party Headquarters will provide guidance and lead the citizens to cooperate to improve the municipality day by day. This is our greatest hope. (End)

Criminal Ruling: Chen Lian Li Zheng's request for bail for his son, Chen Zixun, who is suffering from a critical illness in prison, for medical treatment, has been noted. Upon investigation, Zixun has been suffering from illness in prison and has been sent to the patrol police hospital for treatment. According to the doctor's report, he is still seriously ill. This is consistent with the applicant's statement. In accordance with Article 485, Paragraph 4 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the execution of the sentence is suspended until Chen Zixun recovers from his illness. He shall submit a surety of $700 and then go out for

medical treatment. ▲ Qin Lisan's request to withdraw the private prosecution has been noted. The prosecution in this case is approved for withdrawal. ▲ Wu Yueren and Wu Jianyin's request to re-examine the body of Wu Shunren has been noted. It has been verified by this court that the deceased Wu Shunren committed suicide. Subsequently, the deceased's cousin, Wu Dazhi, requested a re-examination, and this court convened a hearing and determined that there was no suspicion of foul play, and the request for re-examination was denied. Now, the applicants have not submitted any evidence and are merely requesting a re-examination with empty words, which is difficult to approve. There shall be no further disturbance. ▲ Yang Shunyuan, etc., request a continued hearing. Upon investigation, this court has established that a criminal judgment must be appealed within ten days. If an appeal is not filed within the deadline, the judgment becomes final and does not require written service to become effective. The letter states that the finality takes effect only after written service, which is a misunderstanding. Furthermore, when the judgment was announced in this case, it was stated that if there was any objection to the judgment, an appeal could be filed within the appeal period. The applicant did not file an appeal according to law within the appeal period after hearing the judgment but repeatedly petitioned after the judgment became final, which is inappropriate. ▲ Xu Xuezhen requests to withdraw the complaint. The case was previously rejected due to the self-plaintiff's violation of procedure, and the request for withdrawal need not be discussed. ▲ Li Wannian requests the return of the bond in the case of Xu Shaoqiu's complaint of fraud and breach of trust. The case has been appealed by Xu Shaoqiu, and the request need not be discussed. The above is from March 3rd.

Free Talk

A Bit of Insight

— Long

Willingness to suffer losses in everything, and not haggling with others, is where the advantage lies.

The more people who like to take advantage, the more they will be fooled, and the degree of loss is greater than anything else.

Those who oppose you to your face may not have bad intentions. Those who agree with you may not be good people.

If a person can use the courage of suicide to deal with all difficulties, they will surely succeed. The rich pretending to be poor, and the poor pretending to be rich, both have their own dissatisfactions.

The world only knows that friends can only share hardship and not happiness, but does not know that lovers can only share happiness and not hardship.

The more prevalent the right of women to inherit property, the more severe the preference for sons over daughters will become, because it will further arouse the jealousy of fathers and brothers.

When a woman gets engaged to a man, it is best to add a condition to the marriage contract (no desertion midway, otherwise a certain amount of alimony must be paid) to save the judge from embarrassment in the future.

Mr. Tang Weizhi's Love of Daytime Naps

— Xu Wancheng

Mr. Tang Weizhi (Wenzhi), a famous figure in academic circles, is a scholar of Chinese studies. He is from Taicang, Jiangsu. He now lives in seclusion in Xiyi, devoting himself to reading and running schools. The Wuxi National Studies College he runs has achieved excellent results and has been submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval. It is the only excellent school for researchers of national studies. Without Mr. Tang's painstaking management, how could it have reached this point?

Mr. Tang resides in Xixi, Xiyi, with beautiful and serene scenery. There are bamboo groves, large vegetable gardens, and ponds. Birds soar above, and fish swim below. Mr. Tang strolls through it, indulging in relaxation and detachment from the world. This is enough to delight him. Mr. Tang is over sixty years old, yet he is majestic in stature and vigorous in spirit, which is due to his dwelling outside the material world.

Mr. Tang has an extraordinary memory and has extensively studied old texts. He can recite ancient books, possessing a vast knowledge. He also loves daytime naps. Two hours after noon is Mr. Tang's nap time, a habit he never interrupts. Wancheng once worked at the college and was close to him, so he knows this well.

In the Spring and Autumn period, Zai Yu, also known as Zai Wo, a disciple of Confucius from Lu, also liked to sleep during the day (see the Analects). In the Eastern Han Dynasty, Bian Shao, courtesy name Xiaoxian, from Junyi (now northwest of Kaifeng County, Henan), was famous for his literature and quick wit, able to compose poems on the spot and known as the "walking library." He also liked to sleep during the day (see the Book of the Later Han). Therefore, Mr. Tang can be said to be Zai Yu of ancient times and Bian Xiaoxian of modern times.

Impressed Fingerprints in Mud

— Qian

In the town, there was an old man named Gu who practiced the art of picking locks, and his skills were particularly ingenious, so he was never caught. Old Man Gu's hands both had special marks, with an extra little finger next to the thumb, commonly known as six fingers. On the 17th of this month, a Mr. Wu's house in Zhendong suddenly reported a theft. Upon inspection, the stolen items were all of ordinary value, such as copper vegetable knives. However, a pair of mud fingerprints were found on the kitchen wall, clearly showing twelve fingers. It was known to be the work of Old Man Gu, so it was reported to the Public Security Bureau, requesting his arrest. Police officers went to Old Man Gu's house, and Gu was still sleeping soundly. He was dragged out and taken to the bureau, where he was interrogated. Old Man Gu vehemently denied it, saying he hadn't done this for several years and would never leave his fingerprints to arouse suspicion, indicating that someone else had framed him. The bureau chief asked if there were any clues, but for the time being, he was detained in the detention center. Old Man Gu had a daughter who was already twenty-nine years old and engaged to a Mr. Lu from the same town, with plans to marry at the end of this year. After the old man was detained, Mr. Lu felt greatly unfair and ran around seeking help, asking people to speak on their behalf and going to the victim, Mr. Wu, to intercede for his future father-in-law. The old man's daughter also brought copper vegetable knives and other items, returning them to Mr. Wu, saying they were found in her father's room. Mr. Wu, moved by the plea of the engaged couple, felt pity and voluntarily withdrew the charges, releasing the old man. After Old Man Gu was released, he felt exceptionally grateful to Ms. Lu and greatly resented the thief who framed him. The day before yesterday (26th), Old Man Gu agreed to Ms. Lu's request to marry her to Mr. Lu earlier. The next day, his daughter finally told him that the theft from Mr. Wu was done by her fiancé, Mr. Lu. After Mr. Lu became engaged to Old Man Gu's daughter, he became very close and eager to marry. Seeing that Old Man Gu was stubborn and insisted on waiting until the end of the year, he secretly discussed it with Old Man Gu's daughter, plotting this to feign a diligent rescue effort and advance the wedding date. Old Man Gu was shocked and furious upon hearing this, but the rice was already cooked, and there was no turning back. He scolded his daughter and son-in-law a few times and let it go.

Tan Ma Fulu's New Film

— Chongliang

In recent times, talent in the Jingju opera has been most prevalent in the Sheng and Dan roles, as they can cater to current tastes and easily achieve fame. The Jing roles of Shouchen, Shaoshan, and Xirui compete in the north and south, showing a tendency to solely support the giant building and confront the Sheng and Dan. The Chou roles of Changlin, Changhua, Fulu, and Fuhui are also catching up quickly, not willing to lag behind. Their magic power to attract viewers may not be below Hao Jin. It is a pity that Changlin is declining and does not have the vibrant spirit of the past. Fuhui is also a bit young. From now on, the masters and apprentices Changhua and Fulu will be allowed to dominate. Xiao Ma's elegant voice has been gradually accumulated in records, especially Ma's majestic voice and good singing, which is the most popular. A few days ago, I purchased his new records, "Broken Arm Tax Certificate," "Sweeping the Floor and Hanging Pictures," and "Little Shepherd Boy," recorded by Great China, from Desheng Company, which I found quite satisfactory. According to the old woman in "Broken Arm," Luo Fushan is the most stable. Fulu has also worked on this for a long time. The four sentences of the Second Huang Yuanban have a mellow taste, directly surpassing Li Dakui's Woyunjushi. The section of spoken lines is very realistic, which cannot be compared to the current old women who can sing but are not good at acting. The singing in "Sweeping the Floor and Hanging Pictures" follows the Jing role, and it is indeed loud and grand, especially the tune of "Knocking my head to thank Hong'en" is the best. The "Little Shepherd Boy" piece returns to its role as a clown, assisted by Yu Lianxian, a graduate of the Fuliangcheng class, who complements each other. In short, Fulu has a good natural throat, coupled with a clever and intelligent talent, so he can have this talent and artistry. Later clown roles should be regarded as giants.

Record of Gourd Fortune Telling

— Huo

My respectful friend Yan Fusun has long been famous for his literary and artistic achievements, and his gourd calligraphy is especially infused with his heart and soul. Since the Gourd Fortune Telling Center moved to its new location west of the Tianchan Stage, its reputation has grown even more. Yesterday, my relative, Mr. Hu, mentioned Mr. Yan's calligraphy and art, sharing several things that are magical and worth recording. This briefly gives a glimpse.

My friend, Mr. Zhou Wuai, has been an amateur opera enthusiast for many years. A few weeks ago, he was about to go to the capital for a New Year's performance. Nearing the time, he suddenly felt very nervous, fearing he would miss the performance. He shook the two characters (戔勺) in Mr. Yan's gourd. Yan judged, "There is no water beside 戔, so this trip will surely be stranded. And the character 勺 lacks gold, so fishing will not be successful." Zhou was greatly surprised by the judgment, saying, "The play I am practicing is 'Fishing for a Golden Turtle'. I did not expect the gourd's twin pearls to have foresight."

Yu Baiji of Nanshi will contract a construction project in the capital, hoping for its success. Suddenly, an obstacle arose. He rushed to ask for guidance, shaking out the two pearls (其區). Yan immediately judged, ""其" is a foundation without soil, and the fundamental foundation has not been consolidated. The shape of the character "區" is also of a broken gold pot. What is missing on the right is a piece of tile. Without even one tile left, it will eventually fall apart.” Yu carefully examined the meaning of the words and knew that there was no hope. Shortly after the bidding opened, he was indeed not selected.

Friend A and Friend B are in a love rivalry, further alienated by misunderstandings. A went to ask for guidance, shaking the two characters (吳兼). Yan said, "Try to interpret (吳), it means that without a woman, there is no pleasure for the gentleman. Furthermore,"(兼) it is better to be humble in one word. Be humble and give in, otherwise (言) plus (吳) becomes a mistake. (女) plus (兼) becomes a suspicion. If a woman accumulates suspicion and plots treachery from within, the misunderstanding will become even greater and more difficult to resolve." A, upon hearing the judgment, suddenly realized and gave up love, becoming as friendly as before with B. A staff member of Fengshenghang, Mr. Hu, gambled and lost heavily, misappropriating public funds. The business owner was about to file a lawsuit and pursue him. Hu's family, fearing this, went to consult the gourd, shaking the two characters (宛兌). Yan said, (宛) is a sign that the rice bowl has been broken. Although someone has been asked to plead, but with (兌) pushing, there is no word to the mouth. I am afraid that there is nothing to say in the end. As a result, Hu was indeed dismissed.

My friend, Mr. Wang, owed his uncle some private debts. However, the amount was not large, and since he was an elder, he was embarrassed to ask for it repeatedly. When he casually asked about it, he was reprimanded. Recently, he shook out the two characters (歐訴). Yan smiled and said, "There is no need to ask for it, it is a waste of words. Because (歐) clearly states that it is a trivial debt, and (訴) clearly shows that one request leads to a reprimand. The meaning of the words is clearly revealed, and the opportunity is known without pondering." Wang sighed with admiration.

Common Sense Snippets

— Tang Bihua

When riding the tram and it is crowded, you must hold the rattan ring with your left hand and insert your right hand into your pocket. Then, no matter how cunning the pickpocket is, they will not be able to do anything to you.

When renting a house, first check whether there is a brass plate at the door and how the living room is furnished. If there is no brass plate and the living room is messy and disorderly, this kind of sub-landlord cannot be trusted.

Encephalitis is rampant again these days. This disease is most easily spread, especially in public places. To prevent it, you can sprinkle some perfume on your handkerchief and cover your mouth and nose with it while walking, which can avoid danger. It is best to go less often to bathhouses, hotels, restaurants, teahouses, wine shops, and theaters.

When smoking, do not use red-tipped matches, because the phosphorus poison in red-tipped matches is several times higher than in black-tipped matches. It is very dangerous to smoke with them.

Red Rug

Anecdotes of a Tour to America by Zhui Yu Xuan (2)

— Seattle Correspondence

The next day, the overseas Chinese, Jin Ti, hosted a welcome banquet at the Maden Hotel. Acting Consul Liu gave a welcoming speech, with over a hundred guests in attendance. In his speech, he especially praised Wan Hua for promoting the arts, calling it a new record for an art troupe traveling abroad to the United States. That evening, they attended a welcome dinner hosted by the Sino-American Association of Seattle, with participants from over twenty organizations, such as the local Chamber of Commerce, Board of Education, Art Association, City Council, and Railway Bureau, totaling over three hundred seats. After the chairman's speech, Chinese Consul Liu delivered a speech stating that the arrival of a Chinese art troupe in the United States was an unprecedented event. He praised Mei Jun's leadership in leading the troupe across the ocean to promote the arts, stating that their ambition was great, their spirit

resolute, and truly commendable and admirable. He also expressed his delight in participating in such a grand welcome from the American side, for which he also expressed gratitude. Next, Professor Kang Wei of the University of Washington (Professor Kang is a professor of history and Chinese drama at the University of Washington) spoke about the history and advantages of Chinese drama. His knowledge was profound and meticulous, which was truly commendable. In conclusion, he stated that they had heard about Mei Jun's arrival in the United States for many years, and were fortunate to finally see him in person and receive his guidance. This was a great opportunity for those who study Eastern art and drama. He further stated that Mei Jun was not only skilled in performing Chinese dramas, but also able to improve ancient Chinese dramas, bringing them back to the stage, and creating many exquisite and elegant works. This has raised the status of the dramatic arts. Mei Jun possesses such outstanding ideas and talent that he is not only a famous Chinese dramatist, but also deserves to be regarded as the only dramatist in the world. His arrival should not be viewed through the eyes of an ordinary theater troupe, but as an effort to promote Eastern culture and art. How should we express our welcome and gratitude? Next, the president of the local court delivered a speech, quoting a Western philosopher, saying that a person who can use unique art to provide appreciation for the world is truly the happiest person in the world, but it is difficult to achieve. Now that Mei Jun has come to the United States, it has truly been achieved. How fortunate are we, how fortunate is America, to encounter such a rare event in the world? Subsequently, Wan Hua rose to give a response, which was tactful and appropriate. After the speech, the whole place erupted in thunderous applause, and the event dispersed late at night.

On the second day, the Sino-American Progressive Association welcomed the entire troupe to tour the city and invited them to visit the University of Washington. At noon, they attended a tea party hosted by the Chinese students of the university. They all stated that Mei Jun's trip would bring honor to our country and that they would provide all possible assistance. In the evening, they attended an appointment at the local Fifth Avenue Theater. The theater was constructed purely in the Chinese architectural style and was completed two years ago. A portrait of Wan Hua hangs in the main hall, which was requested and sent by the former American Consul in Shanghai before the theater's opening. When Wan Hua arrived, the general manager of the theater respectfully greeted him at the door, personally presenting him with a bouquet of fresh flowers and leading him into the theater. During the performance, someone on stage announced (We are honored to have Mr. Mei Lanfang, a great art promoter from China, visiting us.) to express their welcome. The audience applauded loudly. As the curtain was about to fall, the leading actor of the play also said that Mei Jun was now sitting in the front flower building. Why not focus the lights on him so that the guests could meet each other? Then the lights were turned on brightly, focusing on Wan Hua. Wan stood up and bowed in response, and the audience applauded again and again. Many people came from New York to welcome Wan Hua. Local reporters also came to interview him. As a result, he stayed in Seattle for another day before taking the specially prepared car of the Great Northern Railway east. The send-off was crowded, and they waved their handkerchiefs in farewell as the train whistle sounded and headed towards New York.

Warmth in the Heart (140)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 9: The Celebrated Gentlemen Create Laughter with Hide-and-Seek; The Charming Lady Protects with Abandon. In Ruiyun's heart... she thought that winning a big hand meant a complete victory for herself. Therefore, she developed a habit of showing off her cleverness. As a result, she was always the one winning at mahjong. This was called "eating three" and also "the Two-Two Immortals Returning to the Cave." Ruiyun often used a challenging tone, either at the table or when Shichen went to her place for tea gatherings, saying, "Dare you come again tonight? Are you not afraid of losing more?" Shichen replied, "Of course I'll come. How can I lose to a little kid? I'm definitely coming to get my money back today." Ruiyun said, "Okay, I'll wait for you. Come and get your money back. Bring more money. Wait until you win before talking big." This was Ruiyun's moment of triumphant pride, holding onto her strong confidence, like those warlords in recent times who have won a few battles and think that no one can defeat them, becoming arrogant. However, her mahjong playing was indeed improving. First, she had sharp eyes and quick hands. Sometimes, before others could even discard their tiles, she would say "Faster, faster!" while already drawing a tile from the dealer's pile. Shichen said, "Watching Little Zhang is no use." Ruiyun said, "Who's watching Little Zhang? I never want the tiles discarded by the previous player anyway." In the end, Ruiyun won again. She said triumphantly, "How about it? Did you lose to a little kid again today? Can't an adult win against a little kid?" When it came time to settle the accounts, Hanyun, though she lost, was secretly helping Shichen. When A Jin lost, Ruiyun often didn't ask her to pay, saying it was okay to owe it. "I can deduct it when I lose in the future." Hearing this, A Jin honestly didn't pay. Only Shichen's losses had to be paid. Although the amount was small, they usually played mahjong with a twenty-cent base. Sometimes, they even reduced the stakes to a thousand copper coins. In short, the money Shichen paid was like spoils of war or captured weapons. The next day, she would host guests, inviting people in the room for refreshments, saying it was money won from Second Master Zuo, declaring her victory. But as things went on, it gradually became a habit. If Zuo Shichen didn't come for three days, she would try to call him. Sometimes, with the playful expression of a child, she would say, "I'm out of pocket money these past two days. I have to win some money to use." Shichen also knew that playing mahjong with her was just like giving her money. Fortunately, it was beneficial without being costly. What he liked to see most was Ruiyun winning a big hand. Sometimes, in so-called joyful flips, when a three-flip hand was won, she would often jump up, lean her body on Shichen, or hook her arm around his neck to express her joy. Shichen, however, would just stand there blankly, forgetting all about mahjong, the win or loss, as if his eyes were covered by a mist, only vaguely aware of her charming manner, her clever smile, wavering and unable to control himself.

As for the bond prices, they were still peaceful in the early morning, with slight fluctuations. Except for the Seven-Year Bond and the Ninety-Six Financial Bond, which had small inflows and outflows and only rose by a few cents, the others all rose significantly. The futures and Continued Bonds, and the Tariff Bonds for this month rose by about 1 yuan, and the rest also rose by 5 or 6 cents or so, and the trend was quite uniform.

Yarn and Cotton Market Continues to Be Weak

The yarn market turned tired, but actual sales in the market were more brisk, and various groups showed signs of improvement. Coarse yarn accounted for the majority, but people's hearts could not be stirred, and there were still many people who were bearish. As a result, when the market rose slightly, the selling wind became fierce. This situation was entirely due to the high inventories and rumors of the current situation. Sellers had stronger courage. If the demand for current yarn from various groups could continue, the market might have the power to rise.

The Manchu Standard was Suppressed by American Cotton and Gold Prices. The market sentiment for the Manchu Standard was weaker in the morning opening, because American cotton fell again and retail investors sold out. The prices of each month fell by 2, 5, or 6 cents. The market heard that gold prices had plummeted at two or three o'clock, and the hearts of the people in the market were moved, and it fell another 6 or 7 cents. The closing price rebounded slightly, and each month fell by 6, 7, 8, 9 cents to 1 tael. Although the actual sales route was good in the afternoon, it was still difficult to raise the popularity, and 4,250 bales of No. 40 were sold in large quantities, and the market situation was collapsed again. As a result, it rose by 1, 2, and 4 cents, and the distant month was flat. The total number of transactions for the whole day was 16,800 bales. New York Cotton Exchange's New Rules

▲ Deliveries No Longer in New York

New York, 26th – A New York dispatch states that the New York Cotton Exchange today passed an amendment with provisions, introducing a new type of contract that eliminates deliveries in New York and price differences for deliveries at various Southern ports. The implementation of this amendment will mean that New York will no longer be a delivery location. The new contract is set to take effect on February 27th, starting with the October term. Transactions under the old contract will continue, but after the end of January next year, transactions will be limited to the new contract. Therefore, futures for October, November, December, and January will have two types of contracts until the end of January next year.

English-Indian Cotton Industry Weekly Report

The Bombay cotton market is currently constrained by ample inventories. Broach cotton is more expensive than Gogera and Oomra cotton due to the poor quality of Gogera cotton and upcoming transactions in April and May. However, broadly speaking, Indian cotton remains cheap. If inventories decrease, market prices will undoubtedly be affected. Currently, American cotton is weak, so spot demand in Bombay and Karachi is poor. Local manufacturers are more interested in purchasing Southern cotton. The statistics for the past week are appended below (in thousands of bales):

Accumulated exports since September 1st   1,146   1,204

Exports to Europe     396   418

Exports to China     139   139

Exports to Japan     579   615

Exports to other regions   32   32

Spot sales in Liverpool were very strong last week. Futures prices moved entirely with American cotton. Prices soared, but confidence remains lacking. Egyptian cotton has made slight progress due to government intervention, but largely remains sympathetic to the fluctuations of American cotton.

Japan's Spindle Count Increases by Another 300,000

Japanese yarn factories, in an effort to counter the production issues caused by the abolition of nighttime labor, are actively increasing spindles. As a result, production has surged, leading to a 10% reduction in labor, as reported previously. According to a survey by the Japan Textile Federation, as of the end of December last year, there were 6,648,874 spindles, an increase of 300,1568 spindles compared to the end of June.
