Flour Prices Fall Sharply

Slight Recovery in Northern Flour Before Closing

Future Movements Depend on Foreign Wheat Prices

Yesterday, the flour market experienced price declines, especially for near-term months like March, April, and May. The market was unsettled due to small foreign wheat reports of 5-6 jiao and sharp declines in standard flour prices. Sellers did not offer their goods aggressively, but the market inevitably softened. For example, the lowest price for this month in the afternoon session reached 2.53 yuan, for April 2.5325 yuan, and for May 2.475 yuan, all falling approximately 2 fen compared to the previous week's closing prices. However, in later sessions, most people were wary of repeating the previous week's events, believing that prices would rebound after an easy fall, so they considered it risky to heavily short. Also, slight movement in Northern flour stabilized sentiment, and the market gradually recovered, gaining about 1 fen from the lowest point. However, the final outcome will depend on foreign prices, as speculation among traders seems to have taken on an international character. Consequently, this month's price was down 7.5 li compared to the previous week's closing price, April was down 1 fen, May was down 5 li. Distant-term new flour prices remained stable due to the sudden cold and rain in spring, with June and July remaining unchanged. August, however, was up 2.5 li.

Wheat Futures Trend Lower

Yesterday, after the morning and afternoon opening of the wheat market, prices for all months were generally unstable. Current fluctuations are purely influenced by foreign prices. As foreign wheat reports remained small and standard flour prices fell sharply, market sentiment was uniformly weak, and prices declined steadily. Prices for distant-term new wheat also showed weakness due to low morale. Consequently, this month's morning price was down 2 fen compared to the previous week's closing price, with no afternoon trading. April was down 5 fen, June was down 1 fen, July was down 2 fen, and August was down 3 fen. Spot wheat prices remained stable because the standard had already reached around 1 qian, and customer sentiment was firm. Factories, due to their needs, could not reject the higher prices, so high-quality goods rose by 2-3 fen. Kainansuzhou wheat was priced at 5.15 yuan to 5.13 yuan, Huangqiao wheat at 5.14 yuan, Taizhou wheat at 5.10 yuan, Mingguang wheat at 5.11 yuan to 5.13 yuan, Bengbu wheat at 5.14 yuan, and Shaoxing wheat at 5.08-9 yuan. A total of 5,300 bags were opened, and Fuxin, Zhonghua, Shenda, and other factories purchased them.

Rice Market Scarce and Stable

Yesterday, the sources of various types of rice in Zhabei were scarce, totaling less than 20. Sales in the local market were slightly active, and Northern japonica rice shifted from weak to stable. Sellers initially wanted to raise prices, but buyers refused, resulting in prices remaining the same as the previous session. Arrivals of Bo rice were not strong, and sales were very slow, with little price fluctuation. Yangdu Xian rice from Luliu saw rising prices due to purchases by merchants, so the source was very thin. Ke rice from other ports saw diligent movement due to tight foreign rice supplies, and prices for Ke rice were uniformly firm. Sales of Baiyuan were not brisk, and Dukejian continued to arrive in Shanghai, with prices stagnant and unresponsive.

Few boats arrived in South Shanghai, and market sales were flat. Changxi Sutong and other machine-milled japonica rice saw slightly active sales, with varying buying sentiments in different villages. Upper and middle japonica rice were more active, with no significant price changes. The market for Bozao rice from Southern Qingyong and other regions was sluggish, with weak buying interest and falling prices. Sales of Yangdu Port and other Xian rice were quite successful. Although recent arrivals were low, there was still accumulated stock, resulting in only a slight firmness. Circulation and demand for Yinyuan grains were lackluster, and demand from various merchants was weak, resulting in few transactions and a stable market. Overall, the situation was quieter in South Shanghai than in Zhabei.

Sales of Piece Goods Improve, Prices Rebound

Fine Cloth Soars by Five Fen. The market showed a sudden tightness yesterday, mainly due to the recent sharp rise in the gold market, which led to cotton yarn prices firming. Cotton cloth prices also rose sharply yesterday, with fine cloth being the strongest, rising by about five fen. Trumpet Boy was priced at 6.775 yuan, Blue Double Fish at 7.5 qian, and Hehe at 7.25 qian. Four Army Man sold over 200 pieces due to mobilization by the Sichuan merchants, also priced at 6.75 yuan. Caibao Niuzhuang, Yantai, and Tianjin all saw strong demand and high prices, selling at 6.85 yuan, the highest price this year. Fine Twill also rose, with Blue Double Fish priced at 6.6 yuan and Yanghe at 6.8 yuan. Coarse cloth was up 2.5 fen. Yihua bleached cloth is out of stock.

Over a hundred pieces of Dongse serge purchased by Sichuan merchants were also stimulated by the plummeting silver prices, leading to a slightly firmer market with slightly improved sales. There were letters from the Yangtze River region yesterday stating that Sichuan merchants had already begun purchasing, with over a hundred pieces of Dong cloth being transacted. Huxinting was priced at 1.7 qian, Six Scholars at 1.65 qian, and Ersunfu at 1.625 qian. Hua Biao Han merchants added a significant number of purchases. Fine cloth saw another rise yesterday, with Shile Bird priced at 7.65 yuan, Double Dragon Pearl at 7.525 yuan, and Yanghong Biao up 5 fen. Six-pound Guo Ju was priced at 3.8 yuan and four-pound at 3.15 yuan. However, due to the abundance of local factory goods, calico still trended downwards. Western-style serge and linen yarn became increasingly active, with over forty pieces sold yesterday. Deji Guo Ziyi sold for 2.85 qian, and Tianyou Tianci Caiyuan for 2.9 qian, with transactions also occurring for Xinji Zhongtiao at 2.29 qian.

Metals and American Tinplate Soar

The transaction of American tinplate has been very prosperous recently, but the source is exhausted, and there are frequent instances of supply not meeting demand in the market. Standard prices have therefore risen step by step, and yesterday's market was even stronger. After the guild price rose to 12.5 taels (90 pounds) and 13.25 taels (100 pounds) the day before, general users panicked and rushed to purchase, with the amount of transactions being unprecedented. The solidity of the standard was also unprecedented. It is estimated that a large amount of transactions reached 7-8,000 boxes for the whole day. It is said that most of them are futures, so the future inventory is unlikely to be rich, and the price may continue to rise.

Seafood Squid Sales Stagnant, Price Drops Two Taels

Since the opening rise of the squid market, customers have been actively transacting, and the market has been quite firm. Recently, due to the current situation, demand from various merchants has suddenly decreased, and merchants' inventories lack potential buyers. Therefore, the market has begun to trend downwards. The current asking price for Xiangguan Qiushui goods is 48 taels, Gao Dongshui is 47 taels, ordinary is around 46 taels, Jiayou Pian is 42-3 taels, Qiepo is 35-6 taels, Duizhou Erban goods is 46-7 taels, and Jinshan goods is 46 taels to 42 taels. Compared to last month's market, each has fallen by more than two taels, and demand is very weak, leading to a sluggish market.

Silk and Tea Shandong Silk Sources Gradually Increase

▲ Qingdao Export Goods Public Weighing Tax Case Resolved

Most of the yellow and white silk from Shandong Province is shipped to Shanghai via Qingdao. Previously, due to the local authorities' implementation of an export goods public weighing tax, merchants opposed it and agreed to stop shipping as a countermeasure. As a result, the source of Shandong silk was interrupted. Now that the public weighing tax case has been resolved, Shandong silk is being shipped out in a steady stream. In recent days, regular Qingdao steamships have transported over 300 pieces of yellow and white factory silk. There is strong demand for Shandong yellow factory silk from Britain and France. Yesterday, Dachang and others imported 48 bales, and Ganli imported 30 bales of white factory silk to Shanghai. Prices varied between firm and weak.

▲ Wang Yusheng Executes Accountant Business. Wang Yusheng, a graduate of the Shanghai School of Commerce of the former National Southeast University (now the School of Business of Central University), and currently a faculty member of National Jinan University, is skilled in accounting. He has taught accounting, bookkeeping, and other courses at Jinan University for many years. He now wishes to use his knowledge to serve the public. He received Accountant Certificate No. 41 issued by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on January 23rd of this year and joined the Shanghai Accountants Association in February of this year. He is scheduled to begin executing accountant business on March 1st, 1920, and has hired Wang Xingcun as an assistant, and Wu Jiying, Qian Yaonan, Xu Qijing, Mao Zongwei, and others as assistant staff. The office is temporarily located in the Minsheng Savings Society in Danfengli, Aveny Road, Beinichengqiao, telephone number 17987.
